## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the canonical form of population dynamics ODEs. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth mechanisms such as logistic growth, Allee effects, or more complex ecological dynamics.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (per-capita growth rate increases then decreases)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible sigmoidal growth ODE)
- Time-varying Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-dependent rate)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting)
- Oscillatory forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonally forced logistic)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Rational density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (growth with saturation in per-capita rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturating birth rate minus linear death)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ c*P) indicates density-independent exponential growth regime
- Quadratic term in P (dP_dt ~ c0*P - c1*P^2) signals density-dependent competition or carrying capacity limitation
- Cubic terms in P (dP_dt ~ P*(P-a)*(K-P)) indicate Allee effects with a minimum viable population threshold
- Logarithmic coupling log(P) in growth rate suggests Gompertz-type dynamics where relative growth decays logarithmically
- Fractional powers of P (P^c where 0<c<1) suggest surface-area-to-volume scaling in metabolic growth models
- Time-dependent coefficients or explicit t terms suggest non-autonomous dynamics like seasonal variation or environmental change
- Ratio P/(1+c*P) indicates Holling type II functional response or saturating resource utilization
- Product of multiple linear factors in P indicates multiple equilibria (extinction, Allee threshold, carrying capacity)
- If dP_dt depends only on P (not t), the system is autonomous and phase-line analysis applies with fixed equilibria
- Negative constant terms independent of P suggest constant-rate harvesting or immigration effects
